<a id="19378" class="Comment">-- An element of the poset is like a finite observation whereas an element of the</a>
<a id="19460" class="Comment">-- frame of downward closed posets is like a general observation.</a>

<a id="28837" class="Comment">-- Similar to the poset case, this is sufficient to establish that the category of frames</a>
<a id="28927" class="Comment">-- is univalent</a>

<a id="‚âÉf‚âÉ‚â°"></a><a id="28944" href="Frame.html#28944" class="Function">‚âÉf‚âÉ‚â°</a> <a id="28949" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="28951" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="28952" href="Frame.html#28952" class="Bound">F</a> <a id="28954" href="Frame.html#28954" class="Bound">G</a> <a id="28956" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="28958" href="Frame.html#3701" class="Function">Frame</a> <a id="28964" href="Basis.html#2598" class="Generalizable">‚Ñì‚ÇÄ</a> <a id="28967" href="Basis.html#2601" class="Generalizable">‚Ñì‚ÇÅ</a> <a id="28970" href="Basis.html#2604" class="Generalizable">‚Ñì‚ÇÇ</a><a id="28972" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="28974" class="Symbol">‚Üí</a> <a id="28976" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="28977" href="Frame.html#28952" class="Bound">F</a> <a id="28979" href="Frame.html#26422" class="Function Operator">‚âÉf</a> <a id="28982" href="Frame.html#28954" class="Bound">G</a><a id="28983" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="28985" href="Agda.Builtin.Cubical.Glue.html#1051" class="Function Operator">‚âÉ</a> <a id="28987" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="28988" href="Frame.html#28952" class="Bound">F</a> <a id="28990" href="Agda.Builtin.Cubical.Path.html#381" class="Function Operator">‚â°</a> <a id="28992" href="Frame.html#28954" class="Bound">G</a><a id="28993" class="Symbol">)</a>
<a id="28995" href="Frame.html#28944" class="Function">‚âÉf‚âÉ‚â°</a> <a id="29000" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="29002" href="Cubical.Foundations.SIP.html#4416" class="Function">SIP</a> <a id="29006" href="Frame.html#28711" class="Function">frame-is-univ-str</a>

<a id="29025" class="Comment">-- However, there are two minor issues with this.</a>
<a id="29075" class="Comment">--</a>
<a id="29078" class="Comment">--   1. We do not have to talk about equivalences as we are talking about sets;</a>
<a id="29158" class="Comment">--      isomorphisms are well-behaved in our case as we are dealing with sets.</a>
<a id="29237" class="Comment">--</a>
<a id="29240" class="Comment">--  2. We do not have to require the frame data to be preserved. We can show that any</a>
<a id="29326" class="Comment">--     poset isomorphism preserves the frame operators.</a>
<a id="29382" class="Comment">--</a>
<a id="29385" class="Comment">-- We will therefore strengthen our result to work with the notion of poset isomorphism.</a>

<a id="29475" class="Comment">-- We start by showing the equivalence between ‚âÉf and ‚âÖ‚Çö.</a>

<a id="‚âÉf‚âÉ‚âÖ‚Çö"></a><a id="29534" href="Frame.html#29534" class="Function">‚âÉf‚âÉ‚âÖ‚Çö</a> <a id="29540" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="29542" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="29543" href="Frame.html#29543" class="Bound">F</a> <a id="29545" href="Frame.html#29545" class="Bound">G</a> <a id="29547" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="29549" href="Frame.html#3701" class="Function">Frame</a> <a id="29555" href="Basis.html#2598" class="Generalizable">‚Ñì‚ÇÄ</a> <a id="29558" href="Basis.html#2601" class="Generalizable">‚Ñì‚ÇÅ</a> <a id="29561" href="Basis.html#2604" class="Generalizable">‚Ñì‚ÇÇ</a><a id="29563" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="29565" class="Symbol">‚Üí</a> <a id="29567" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="29568" href="Frame.html#3968" class="Function">pos</a> <a id="29572" href="Frame.html#29543" class="Bound">F</a> <a id="29574" href="Poset.html#15650" class="Function Operator">‚âÖ‚Çö</a> <a id="29577" href="Frame.html#3968" class="Function">pos</a> <a id="29581" href="Frame.html#29545" class="Bound">G</a><a id="29582" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="29584" href="Agda.Builtin.Cubical.Glue.html#1051" class="Function Operator">‚âÉ</a> <a id="29586" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="29587" href="Frame.html#29543" class="Bound">F</a> <a id="29589" href="Frame.html#26422" class="Function Operator">‚âÉf</a> <a id="29592" href="Frame.html#29545" class="Bound">G</a><a id="29593" class="Symbol">)</a>

  <a id="29658" class="Keyword">where</a>
    <a id="29668" href="Frame.html#29668" class="Function">to</a> <a id="29671" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="29673" href="Frame.html#29601" class="Bound">F</a> <a id="29675" href="Frame.html#26422" class="Function Operator">‚âÉf</a> <a id="29678" href="Frame.html#29603" class="Bound">G</a> <a id="29680" class="Symbol">‚Üí</a> <a id="29682" href="Frame.html#3968" class="Function">pos</a> <a id="29686" href="Frame.html#29601" class="Bound">F</a> <a id="29688" href="Poset.html#15650" class="Function Operator">‚âÖ‚Çö</a> <a id="29691" href="Frame.html#3968" class="Function">pos</a> <a id="29695" href="Frame.html#29603" class="Bound">G</a>
    <a id="29701" href="Frame.html#29668" class="Function">to</a> <a id="29704" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="29705" href="Frame.html#29705" class="Bound">e</a><a id="29706" class="Symbol">@(</a><a id="29708" href="Frame.html#29708" class="Bound">f</a> <a id="29710" href="Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#236" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="29712" class="Symbol">_)</a> <a id="29715" href="Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#236" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="29717" href="Frame.html#29717" class="Bound">f-mono</a> <a id="29724" href="Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#236" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="29726" href="Frame.html#29726" class="Bound">g-mono</a> <a id="29733" href="Agda.Builtin.Sigma.html#236" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="29735" class="Symbol">_)</a> <a id="29738" class="Symbol">=</a>

<a id="34976" class="Comment">-- Now that we have this result, we can move on to show that given two frames F and G,</a>
<a id="35063" class="Comment">-- (pos F) ‚âÖ‚Çö (pos G) is equivalent to F ‚â° G.</a>
